Australian home should be given energy performance rating: report A new joint report by the Property Council of Australia and the Green Building Council of Australia calls for every Australian home to be given an energy performance rating, allowing buyers or renters to know the energy efficiency of their home before moving in. The Every Building Counts report was launched in Sydney today and sets out a suite of property-focused policy recommendations that would help Australia achieve its decarbonisation goals. Among the report’s 39 recommendations is the creation of a national rating scheme for the energy performance of homes, similar to white goods and electronic appliances.\nLabor has already revealed the federal budget will include funding to expand and upgrade the Nationwide House Energy Rating Scheme, which allows people to understand the energy performance of their home. The tool will be upgraded to apply to existing homes, not just new homes. review.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;,&quot;elementId&quot;:&quot;05e9ada8-6669-4b2c-b559-fb94e2abccd4&quot;},{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.TextBlockElement&quot;,&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;p&gt;She harks back to Labor’s history on migration history: a “gutsy” &lt;strong&gt;Ben Chifley&lt;/strong&gt; warning that we must “populate or perish” in the 1940s, &lt;strong&gt;Gough Whitlam&lt;/strong&gt; in the 1970s blowing open the “dusty doors of power to bury the white Australia policy as well as &lt;strong&gt;Paul Keating&lt;/strong&gt; using skilled migration to drive Australia out of recession.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;,&quot;elementId&quot;:&quot;a4bdef26-c972-4962-80b4-fc06aaaa5fdd&quot;},{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.TextBlockElement&quot;,&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;p&gt;She tells the audience in Canberra:&lt;/p&gt;&quot;,&quot;elementId&quot;:&quot;3c70cb9f-2db0-43aa-9914-19157154b7c1&quot;},{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.BlockquoteBlockElement&quot;,&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;blockquote class=\&quot;quoted\&quot;&gt;\n &lt;p&gt;Today I want to have a conversation about migration which is direct and honest. In each of these historic instances migration helped us become a more prosperous and secure Australia because the system was designed to meet the challenges of the moment.&lt;/p&gt;\n &lt;p&gt;And that is not true of our system today. I would challenge anyone in this room to explain what national problems our migration system is seeking to solve.&lt;/p&gt;\n &lt;p&gt;Our migration system is suffering from a decade of genuinely breathtaking neglect. &lt;strong&gt;It is broken, it is failing our businesses and failing migrants themselves and, most important of all, it is failing Australians.&lt;/strong&gt; And that cannot continue because we as a country face some big national challenges migration can help us change Australian Electoral Commission says it is concerned about misinformation and disinformation around the Indigenous Voice referendum, planning a “significant” series of information campaigns to stamp out falsehoods about the voting process.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;,&quot;elementId&quot;:&quot;0f8b0ee8-3651-4f2a-8476-a28d4f272c49&quot;},{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.TextBlockElement&quot;,&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;p&gt;The AEC gave a media briefing this morning in Parliament House, ahead of the referendum to be held later this year (mid-October is seen as a likely option). Commissioner &lt;strong&gt;Tom Rogers&lt;/strong&gt; stressed the AEC’s role was to monitor misinformation and disinformation around the electoral process only, and would not weigh in on the content of the referendum – that is, they would for instance talk about how votes can be cast and how the referendum is decided, but not fact-check legal claims about how the Indigenous voice would operate or what it would do.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;,&quot;elementId&quot;:&quot;d4b9df90-2e69-469e-b728-dc1edded5b71&quot;},{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.TextBlockElement&quot;,&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;p&gt;The AEC is already running information campaigns on Twitter, Facebook, YouTube and platforms such as Reddit. Rogers said the commission was already seeing a lot of previously debunked falsehoods around the electoral process, including claims about Dominion voting machines (which are not used in Australia), as well as people misunderstanding the rules of the referendum.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;,&quot;elementId&quot;:&quot;05f64e83-eecb-45ed-81d3-ecefe279361d&quot;},{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.TextBlockElement&quot;,&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;p&gt;He said the AEC was concerned some voters may confuse the rules of the marriage equality postal survey in 2017 with the rules of a referendum. Unlike the postal survey, it is compulsory to vote in a referendum; the result is binding; and most people will end up voting in-person, not via the post.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;,&quot;elementId&quot;:&quot;f7c7a4fe-a2aa-4f81-81ff-f67de6bf035a&quot;},{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.TextBlockElement&quot;,&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;p&gt;There are also the same rules as at a federal election, including that voting is compulsory (lest you face a $20 fine). Rogers said national enrolment was hovering around 97%, with Indigenous enrolment around 84.5%.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;,&quot;elementId&quot;:&quot;b7310c10-052d-4a2a-b865-861763a4634c&quot;},{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.TextBlockElement&quot;,&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;p&gt;Rogers also stressed there may not be a definitive result in the referendum on the night of the vote. Remember, a referendum is run differently to a federal election – to pass, the vote requires a national majority of support on a national basis, and a majority of voters in a majority of states (that is, four of the six states).&lt;/p&gt;&quot;,&quot;elementId&quot;:&quot;0cb70439-5f31-4fbb-821f-f4e43a326d22&quot;},{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.TextBlockElement&quot;,&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;p&gt;The AEC will publish results on a rolling basis through the night, once polls close at 6pm, just like a standard election – with results to be displayed on their website on a national count, a state-by-state count, plus by polling booth and electorate.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;,&quot;elementId&quot;:&quot;1f5aac91-2b87-4665-9480-a06ed6fb7941&quot;},{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.TextBlockElement&quot;,&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;p&gt;There overall figure also includes $1bn for land and joint estate capabilities. Townsville.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;,&quot;elementId&quot;:&quot;08c1fb33-f5f5-42a2-996c-942642b01bb7&quot;},{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.TextBlockElement&quot;,&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;p&gt;The government will also pledge maritime estate investments of $600m, including for additional work at HMAS Coonawarra in the Northern Territory, upgrades to HMAS Cairns, and redevelopment of the Harold E Holt Naval Communications Station in Western Australia.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;,&quot;elementId&quot;:&quot;4cd2d71c-5506-447e-b33b-a2294e9b7cd2&quot;},{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.TextBlockElement&quot;,&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;p&gt;The fine print is that the $3.8bn in funding comes through a combination of $3.6bn reprioritised from other now lower priority defence estate projects and $200m from other cancelled or adjusted defence data-ignore="global-link-styling" class="dcr-18ove8v"><span class="dcr-11d479j">04.47 BST</span></a></div><h2 class="dcr-e6uddv">Debt means government ‘not in the position’ to do everything within first year, PM says</h2><div class="dcr-dzkvsd"><div class="dcr-uae6pk"><img src="https://i.guim.co.uk/img/uploads/2022/05/27/Joe_Hinchliffe.png?width=300&amp;quality=85&amp;auto=format&amp;fit=max&amp;s=30441776d2f4562009af530bb6be33a4" alt="Eden Gillespie" class="dcr-1gn8rvs"/></div><span class="dcr-17bj29p">Eden Gillespie</span></div></header><p class="dcr-n6w1lc">Questioned on income support payments, the prime minister, <strong>Anthony Albanese</strong>, says the federal government is currently “not in the position” to do everything within its first year, after inheriting “trillions of dollars of debt”.</p><p class="dcr-n6w1lc">Albanese told reporters the government is doing all it can to drive productivity and will reassess income support payments down the track.</p><blockquote class="dcr-27353m"><p><style data-emotion="css cumn2r">.css-cumn2r{height:1em;width:1.5em;margin-right:3px;vertical-align:baseline;fill:#C70000;}</style><svg viewBox="4 4 24 16" class="css-cumn2r"><path d="M9.2776 8H14.0473C13.4732 12.5489 12.9653 17.0095 12.7445 22H4C4.79495 17.142 6.4511 12.5489 9.2776 8ZM20.3852 8H25.0887C24.5808 12.5489 24.0067 17.0095 23.7859 22H15.0635C15.9688 17.142 17.5587 12.5489 20.3852 8Z"></path></svg>The issue of people’s payments is one that the federal government is looking at.</p> <p>We have a budget in a couple of weeks’ time, but we aren’t in a position, with the trillion dollars of debt that we inherited, to do everything within our first year to address the inadequacy of the former government.</p> <p>But what we are doing is working with business to drive productivity.</p></blockquote><figure id="f58bda65-128e-4fb6-b76a-d2961772ed38" data-spacefinder-role="inline" Canberra:&lt;/p&gt;&quot;,&quot;elementId&quot;:&quot;3c70cb9f-2db0-43aa-9914-19157154b7c1&quot;},{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.BlockquoteBlockElement&quot;,&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;blockquote class=\&quot;quoted\&quot;&gt;\n &lt;p&gt;Today I want to have a conversation about migration which is direct and honest. In each of these historic instances migration helped us become a more prosperous and secure Australia because the system was designed to meet the challenges of the moment.&lt;/p&gt;\n &lt;p&gt;And that is not true of our system today. I would challenge anyone in this room to explain what national problems our migration system is seeking to solve.&lt;/p&gt;\n &lt;p&gt;Our migration system is suffering from a decade of genuinely breathtaking neglect. &lt;strong&gt;It is broken, it is failing our businesses and failing migrants themselves and, most important of all, it is failing Australians.&lt;/strong&gt; And that cannot continue because we as a country face some big national challenges migration can help us change process.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;,&quot;elementId&quot;:&quot;0f8b0ee8-3651-4f2a-8476-a28d4f272c49&quot;},{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.TextBlockElement&quot;,&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;p&gt;The AEC gave a media briefing this morning in Parliament House, ahead of the referendum to be held later this year (mid-October is seen as a likely option). Commissioner &lt;strong&gt;Tom Rogers&lt;/strong&gt; stressed the AEC’s role was to monitor misinformation and disinformation around the electoral process only, and would not weigh in on the content of the referendum – that is, they would for instance talk about how votes can be cast and how the referendum is decided, but not fact-check legal claims about how the Indigenous voice would operate or what it would do.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;,&quot;elementId&quot;:&quot;d4b9df90-2e69-469e-b728-dc1edded5b71&quot;},{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.TextBlockElement&quot;,&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;p&gt;The AEC is already running information campaigns on Twitter, Facebook, YouTube and platforms such as Reddit. Rogers said the commission was already seeing a lot of previously debunked falsehoods around the electoral process, including claims about Dominion voting machines (which are not used in Australia), as well as people misunderstanding the rules of the referendum.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;,&quot;elementId&quot;:&quot;05f64e83-eecb-45ed-81d3-ecefe279361d&quot;},{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.TextBlockElement&quot;,&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;p&gt;He said the AEC was concerned some voters may confuse the rules of the marriage equality postal survey in 2017 with the rules of a referendum. Unlike the postal survey, it is compulsory to vote in a referendum; the result is binding; and most people will end up voting in-person, not via the post.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;,&quot;elementId&quot;:&quot;f7c7a4fe-a2aa-4f81-81ff-f67de6bf035a&quot;},{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.TextBlockElement&quot;,&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;p&gt;There are also the same rules as at a federal election, including that voting is compulsory (lest you face a $20 fine). Rogers said national enrolment was hovering around 97%, with Indigenous enrolment around 84.5%.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;,&quot;elementId&quot;:&quot;b7310c10-052d-4a2a-b865-861763a4634c&quot;},{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.TextBlockElement&quot;,&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;p&gt;Rogers also stressed there may not be a definitive result in the referendum on the night of the vote. Remember, a referendum is run differently to a federal election – to pass, the vote requires a national majority of support on a national basis, and a majority of voters in a majority of states (that is, four of the six states).&lt;/p&gt;&quot;,&quot;elementId&quot;:&quot;0cb70439-5f31-4fbb-821f-f4e43a326d22&quot;},{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.TextBlockElement&quot;,&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;p&gt;The AEC will publish results on a rolling basis through the night, once polls close at 6pm, just like a standard election – with results to be displayed on their website on a national count, a state-by-state count, plus by polling booth and electorate.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;,&quot;elementId&quot;:&quot;1f5aac91-2b87-4665-9480-a06ed6fb7941&quot;},{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.TextBlockElement&quot;,&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;p&gt;There will be a lot of of Australia’s top 10 most advantaged local government areas (LGA) are clustered in Sydney, while the 10 most disadvantaged areas are spread across Queensland and the Northern Territory, new &lt;strong&gt;Woollahra&lt;/strong&gt; in Sydney’s inner-east is the nation’s most advantaged LGA, while &lt;strong&gt;Woorabinda&lt;/strong&gt;, which is 170km south-west of Rockhampton in Central Queensland is the most disadvantaged. &lt;br&gt;&lt;br&gt;The top 10 most advantaged LGAs in Australia in order are: Woollahra (NSW), Mosman (NSW), Ku-ring-gai (NSW), Darwin Waterfront Precinct (NT), North Sydney (NSW), Waverley (NSW), Lane Cove (NSW), Peppermint Grove (WA), Nedlands (WA) and Cottesloe (WA).&lt;br&gt;&lt;br&gt;The 10 most disadvantaged LGAs in Australia in order are: Woorabinda (QLD), Cherbourg (QLD), Belyuen (NT), West Daly (NT), Yarrabah (QLD), Kowanyama (QLD), Wujal Wujal (QLD), East Arnhem (NT), Doomadgee (QLD) and Central Desert The footage, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.abc.net.au/news/2023-03-27/pork-industry-carbon-dioxide-stunning-hidden-cameras-730/102094548\&quot;&gt;first aired by the ABC&lt;/a&gt;, showed pigs writhing, gasping for air, screaming and frothing at the mouth while locked in packed cage gondolas.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;,&quot;elementId&quot;:&quot;886e9e8b-cbf4-4b76-a1aa-e33c730f49cd&quot;},{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.TextBlockElement&quot;,&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;p&gt;The &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.abc.net.au/news/2023-04-26/pig-abattoir-ceases-operations-amid-investigation-allegations/102264842\&quot;&gt;ABC reported on Wednesday&lt;/a&gt; that one of the slaughterhouses depicted in the footage, operated by Australian Food Group, has now &lt;strong&gt;closed amid an investigation by the government regulator PrimeSafe&lt;/strong&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;,&quot;elementId&quot;:&quot;2d429ff1-cea7-4796-9e9e-b1afe5973089&quot;},{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.TextBlockElement&quot;,&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;p&gt;The executive director of Farm Transparency Project, &lt;strong&gt;Chris Delforce&lt;/strong&gt;, described the closure as a “massive win for pigs”.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;,&quot;elementId&quot;:&quot;7923b5cf-81b9-4c39-8dfe-f77f96fd072f&quot;},{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.BlockquoteBlockElement&quot;,&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;blockquote class=\&quot;quoted\&quot;&gt;\n &lt;p&gt;For decades now the Australian pork industry has held up gassing pigs to death as the gold standard in ‘humane’ pig slaughter. Despite numerous reports and investigations proving exactly the opposite, it took me hiding myself inside one of these horrific gas chambers in order to finally reveal this to a mainstream audience and start a long overdue national conversation about the way we treat farmed class=\&quot;quoted\&quot;&gt;\n &lt;p&gt;Around 11 o’clock last night, we were sitting at the bar and there was an Oscar Oscar Oscar call put across the intercom, and that is the man overboard signal.&lt;/p&gt;\n &lt;p&gt;… We were told the ship was turning around, and we were all to go back to our cabins, to make sure all of our party were accounted for.&lt;/p&gt;\n &lt;p&gt;Then the ship deployed the ribs, which are like the little lifeboat type boats, and they had spotlights out in the water. This went on for about an hour.&lt;/p&gt;\n &lt;p&gt;Eventually they started calling a person’s name, it was a male, because the person’s name [was sad] several times so we assumed this person is the missing person. But &lt;strong&gt;this morning there has been no notification from the ship at all as to what’s happened.&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n&lt;/blockquote&gt;&quot;,&quot;elementId&quot;:&quot;40549fc4-dd8d-44a7-8517-a36163314458&quot;}],&quot;attributes&quot;:{&quot;pinned&quot;:false,&quot;keyEvent&quot;:true,&quot;summary&quot;:false},&quot;blockCreatedOn&quot;:1682552468000,&quot;blockCreatedOnDisplay&quot;:&quot;00.41 BST&quot;,&quot;blockLastUpdated&quot;:1682553609000,&quot;blockLastUpdatedDisplay&quot;:&quot;01.00 BST&quot;,&quot;blockFirstPublished&quot;:1682552993000,&quot;blockFirstPublishedDisplay&quot;:&quot;00.49 BST&quot;,&quot;blockFirstPublishedDisplayNoTimezone&quot;:&quot;00.49&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;‘They had spotlights in the water’: cruise passenger tells of frantic search for overboard Australian&quot;,&quot;contributors&quot;:[],&quot;primaryDateLine&quot;:&quot;Thu 27 Apr 2023 07.18 BST&quot;,&quot;secondaryDateLine&quot;:&quot;First published on Wed 26 Apr 2023 21.34 BST&quot;},{&quot;id&quot;:&quot;6449a5c78f08e51b9ca01099&quot;,&quot;elements&quot;:[{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.TextBlockElement&quot;,&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;p&gt;Circling back to finance minister &lt;strong&gt;Katy Gallagher&lt;/strong&gt;’s interview on ABC Radio. You still have to feed them right?&lt;/p&gt;\n&lt;/blockquote&gt;&quot;,&quot;elementId&quot;:&quot;043a971f-43bf-4a88-9201-4830d77984a9&quot;},{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.TextBlockElement&quot;,&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;p&gt;Gallagher:&lt;/p&gt;&quot;,&quot;elementId&quot;:&quot;161629e3-1e37-4ef2-bd8e-d0b1d1428288&quot;},{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.BlockquoteBlockElement&quot;,&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;blockquote class=\&quot;quoted\&quot;&gt;\n &lt;p&gt;Yeah, and you’re right, I did live on that payment. &lt;strong&gt;It changed my life. It saved me.&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n &lt;p&gt;It gave me the support I needed to, to get myself together to look after my baby and to get back into work. So I&lt;strong&gt; 100% understand the importance of these payments&lt;/strong&gt;. class="dcr-11d479j">07.18 BST</span></a></div></header><p class="dcr-n6w1lc">Leader of the Nationals <strong>David Littleproud</strong> has issued a statement saying that regional and rural areas risk being left behind in migration reform announced today.</p><p class="dcr-n6w1lc">He said the federal government’s reforms of the migration system are “a start”, but lack a “clear strategy” to combat widespread worker shortages in the regions.</p><blockquote class="dcr-27353m"><p><style data-emotion="css introduced the dedicated Agriculture Visa, which would have helped alleviate the severe worker shortages that regional Australia, and the entire supply chain, is currently facing, while also creating a new pathway for permanent residency through the Ag Visa.</p></blockquote><p class="dcr-n6w1lc">Littleproud called the government’s decision to scrap the Ag Visa “unconscionable” and “a massive kick href="https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/live/2023/apr/27/australia-news-live-migration-review-defence-budget-labor-coalition-sydney-melbourne-housing-crisis-jobseeker-aged-care?page=with:block-644a0c618f0802b5b51df15b#block-644a0c618f0802b5b51df15b" data-ignore="global-link-styling" class="dcr-18ove8v"><time dateTime="2023-04-27T06:01:37.000Z" data-relativeformat="med" class="dcr-1rl1qsn">18m ago</time><span class="dcr-11d479j">07.01 BST</span></a></div></header><p class="dcr-n6w1lc"><strong>Every Australian home should be given energy performance rating: report</strong></p><p class="dcr-n6w1lc">A new joint report by the Property Council of Australia and the Green Building Council of Australia calls for every Australian home to be given an energy performance rating, allowing buyers or renters to know the energy efficiency of their home before moving in.</p><p class="dcr-n6w1lc">The Every Building Counts report was launched in Sydney today and sets out a suite of property-focused policy recommendations that would help Australia achieve its decarbonisation goals.</p><p class="dcr-n6w1lc">Among the report’s 39 recommendations is the creation of a national rating scheme for the energy performance of homes, similar to white goods and electronic appliances.</p><figure id="6d9fbbb0-0eca-44f8-a8cf-61b33fbd2237" data-spacefinder-role="inline" data-spacefinder-type="model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.TweetBlockElement" class=" dcr-173mewl"><gu-island name="TweetBlockComponent" deferUntil="visible" props="{&quot;element&quot;:{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.TweetBlockElement&quot;,&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;blockquote class=\&quot;nojs-tweet\&quot;&gt;&lt;p lang=\&quot;en\&quot; dir=\&quot;ltr\&quot;&gt;The &lt;a href=\&quot;https://twitter.com/PropertyCouncil?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\&quot;&gt;@PropertyCouncil&lt;/a&gt;&amp;#39;s new report “Every Building Counts” brings together recommendations about the energy performance of our buildings, and outlines the importance of a national energy rating system to ensure healthier and more resilient homes. &lt;a href=\&quot;https://t.co/qjDBghFisw\&quot;&gt;pic.twitter.com/qjDBghFisw&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&amp;mdash; Senator Jenny McAllister (@jennymcallister) &lt;a href="https://twitter.com/PropertyCouncil?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">@PropertyCouncil</a>&#39;s new report “Every Building Counts” brings together recommendations about the energy performance of our buildings, and outlines the importance of a national energy rating system to ensure healthier and more resilient homes. <a href="https://t.co/qjDBghFisw">pic.twitter.com/qjDBghFisw</a></p>&mdash; Senator Jenny McAllister (@jennymcallister) <a href="https://twitter.com/jennymcallister/status/1651461185110446080?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">April 27, 2023</a></blockquote></div></gu-island></figure><p class="dcr-n6w1lc">Labor has already revealed the federal budget will include funding to expand and upgrade the Nationwide House Energy Rating Scheme, which allows people to understand the energy performance of their home.</p><p class="dcr-n6w1lc">The tool will be upgraded to apply to existing homes, not just new homes.</p><p class="dcr-n6w1lc">At a doorstop in Sydney today, assistant minister for climate change and energy <strong>Jenny McAllister</strong> said:</p><blockquote class="dcr-27353m"><p><style data-emotion="css cumn2r">.css-cumn2r{height:1em;width:1.5em;margin-right:3px;vertical-align:baseline;fill:#C70000;}</style><svg viewBox="4 4 24 16" class="css-cumn2r"><path d="M9.2776 8H14.0473C13.4732 12.5489 12.9653 17.0095 12.7445 22H4C4.79495 17.142 6.4511 12.5489 9.2776 8ZM20.3852 8H25.0887C24.5808 12.5489 24.0067 17.0095 23.7859 22H15.0635C15.9688 17.142 17.5587 12.5489 20.3852 8Z"></path></svg>Many [homes] are decades old, but practically, a homeowner would ask an accredited assessor to come to their house and assess … the energy performance of their home.</p> <p>That’ll also give them the information Taylor</strong> (nee Perry) has sold and designed her clothing line under her Katie Perry label since 2007 after being inspired by a trip to Italy.</p><p class="dcr-n6w1lc">While singer <strong>Katheryn Hudson</strong>, more popularly known as <strong>Katy Perry</strong>, initially fought the Australian registration of the Katie Perry brand, she later withdrew this opposition and the mark was registered.</p><p class="dcr-n6w1lc">Taylor sued Hudson for infringement in the federal court in October 2019, more than 10 years after the singer started selling her own brand of merchandise including clothing under her own name.</p><p class="dcr-n6w1lc">Justice <strong>Brigitte Markovic</strong> wrote in a judgment published on Thursday:</p><blockquote class="dcr-27353m"><p><style data-emotion="css cumn2r">.css-cumn2r{height:1em;width:1.5em;margin-right:3px;vertical-align:baseline;fill:#C70000;}</style><svg viewBox="4 4 24 16" class="css-cumn2r"><path d="M9.2776 say</strong></p><p class="dcr-n6w1lc">A second Greens senator has slammed the federal government for reportedly providing funding for an AFL stadium at Macquarie Point in Hobart, Tasmania.</p><p class="dcr-n6w1lc">Tasmanian senator <strong>Nick McKim</strong> said on social media:</p><blockquote class="dcr-27353m"><p><style data-emotion="css the least affordable rents and the fastest increase in homelessness in the country. But instead of supporting the Greens’ plan to fix housing and renting, <strong>Anthony Albanese</strong> plans to give $240 million for a footy stadium.</p></blockquote><p class="dcr-n6w1lc">According to <a href="https://www.theage.com.au/sport/afl/federal-funding-for-hobart-stadium-to-be-announced-on-weekend-paving-way-for-afl-licence-20230425-p5d363.html" data-link-name="in body link">the Age</a>, the $715m stadium would receive $240m in federal funding (set to be announced this weekend), $275m from the state government and $15m from the AFL, with the rest to come from commercial deals.</p><p class="dcr-n6w1lc">McKim argued that Tasmania is on the frontline of Australia’s rental and housing crisis and that this needs urgent attention.</p><blockquote class="dcr-27353m"><p><style data-emotion="css cumn2r">.css-cumn2r{height:1em;width:1.5em;margin-right:3px;vertical-align:baseline;fill:#C70000;}</style><svg viewBox="4 4 24 16" class="css-cumn2r"><path d="M9.2776 8H14.0473C13.4732 12.5489 12.9653 17.0095 12.7445 22H4C4.79495 17.142 6.4511 12.5489 9.2776 8ZM20.3852 8H25.0887C24.5808 12.5489 24.0067 17.0095 23.7859 22H15.0635C15.9688 17.142 17.5587 12.5489 20.3852 8Z"></path></svg>[Albanese] should get cabinet to agree to freeze rents at tomorrow’s meeting, double rent assistance and build 225,000 houses nationally over the next decade. Fund this by [reining] in tax breaks for property speculators. Work with the Greens and this could pass parliament within weeks.</p></blockquote><p class="dcr-n6w1lc">Earlier today, the Greens senator <strong>Peter Whish-Wilson </strong>argued Tasmania’s self-determination has been “sold out” and that the prime minister must answer to Tasmanians “who are sleeping rough or struggling to put food on the table”.</p><footer class="dcr-3i7iba"><ul data-ignore="global-link-styling" class="dcr-18ove8v"><time dateTime="2023-04-27T04:57:01.000Z" data-relativeformat="med" class="dcr-1rl1qsn">1h ago</time><span class="dcr-11d479j">05.57 BST</span></a></div></header><p class="dcr-n6w1lc"><strong>Peak body for skills training and higher education welcomes migration system review</strong></p><p class="dcr-n6w1lc">The Independent Tertiary Education Council Australia has welcomed the government’s review of Australia’s migration system.</p><p class="dcr-n6w1lc">Because independent skills training and higher education providers (which Iteca represents) support more than half of the onshore international student enrolments, the government’s announcements are critical for Iteca members.</p><p class="dcr-n6w1lc">The chief executive, <strong>Troy Williams,</strong> said students needed simple pathways to stay in Australia if they have the skills and capabilities that businesses need.</p><p class="dcr-n6w1lc">The linkages between international education and addressing Australia’s skills needs are critical areas of reform, according to Iteca. Williams said:</p><blockquote class="dcr-27353m"><p><style data-emotion="css cumn2r">.css-cumn2r{height:1em;width:1.5em;margin-right:3px;vertical-align:baseline;fill:#C70000;}</style><svg viewBox="4 4 24 16" class="css-cumn2r"><path d="M9.2776 8H14.0473C13.4732 12.5489 12.9653 17.0095 12.7445 22H4C4.79495 17.142 6.4511 12.5489 9.2776 8ZM20.3852 8H25.0887C24.5808 12.5489 24.0067 17.0095 23.7859 22H15.0635C15.9688 17.142 17.5587 12.5489 20.3852 8Z"></path></svg>From the perspective of the international education sector, it’s great to see a commitment to closer alignment of the nation’s skills needs and international education.</p> <p>The minister is correct to say that the migration system will never be a substitute for adequately skilling Australian workers, but there are also benefits in leveraging the skills of international students in Australia with the education and skills our economy needs.</p></blockquote><p class="dcr-n6w1lc">Williams said that international students are often “baffled” by “too many visa categories and lengthy processing arrangements” that produce “inconsistent outcomes”.</p><blockquote class="dcr-27353m"><p><style data-emotion="css cumn2r">.css-cumn2r{height:1em;width:1.5em;margin-right:3px;vertical-align:baseline;fill:#C70000;}</style><svg viewBox="4 4 24 16" class="css-cumn2r"><path d="M9.2776 8H14.0473C13.4732 12.5489 12.9653 welcome a more transparent and less complicated system.</p></blockquote><p class="dcr-n6w1lc">Iteca says it will work with the government as issues associated with implementing the recommendations are
